      <p><b>Cyril Suk III</b> (born 29 January 1967) is a former professional <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> player. A doubles specialist, Suk won one <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> men's doubles title and four Grand Slam mixed doubles titles during his career. </p>
      <p>Suk was born in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, a member of a prominent Czech tennis family. His mother, <a href="/wiki/V%C4%9Bra_Sukov%C3%A1" title="Věra Suková">Věra Suková</a>, was a women's singles finalist at <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">Wimbledon</a> in 1962. His father, Cyril Suk II, was President of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Czechoslovak_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Czechoslovak Tennis Federation (page does not exist)">Czechoslovak Tennis Federation</a>. His sister, <a href="/wiki/Helena_Sukov%C3%A1" title="Helena Suková">Helena Suková</a>, was an even more successful professional player on the women's tour who teamed-up with Suk to win three Grand Slam mixed doubles titles in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1985, Suk partnered fellow-Czech <a href="/wiki/Petr_Korda" title="Petr Korda">Petr Korda</a> to win the boys' doubles title at the French Open. Suk and Korda were ranked the joint-World No. 1 junior doubles players that year. </p>
      <p>Suk claimed his first Grand Slam mixed doubles title in 1991 at the French Open, partnering sister Helena. In 1992, he teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Larisa_Neiland" title="Larisa Neiland">Larisa Neiland</a> to win the Wimbledon mixed doubles title. He went on to win the Wimbledon mixed doubles crown on two further occasions partnering Helena – in 1996 and 1997. In 1998, Suk teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Sandon_Stolle" title="Sandon Stolle">Sandon Stolle</a> to win the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Open_(tennis)" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Open (tennis)">US Open</a> men's doubles title. </p>
      <p>Suk's career-high doubles ranking was World No. 7 in 1994. (In singles, his career-high ranking was World No. 180 in 1988. He has largely focused on doubles play during his career.) </p>
      <p>Suk was selected as captain of the Czech Republic's <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a> team for the 2003 season. </p>
      <p>Suk married his wife Lenka in 1991. They have a son, Cyril IV (born 1992), and a daughter, Natalie Mia (born 1996). </p>
